## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and current population P, which is the fundamental problem in population dynamics. Classical models relate growth rate to population size through various nonlinear mechanisms like density-dependent feedback, carrying capacity limits, and Allee effects.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Malthusian (exponential) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, constant per-capita rate)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth common in tumor/biological systems)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with flexible inflection point)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance model)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized growth curve)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractal or allometric growth scaling)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (quadratic density effect)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order Allee-type effects)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * t) (time-varying carrying capacity or growth rate)
- Exponentially decaying growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P (time-dependent per-capita rate)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (hyperbolic density dependence)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (constant-effort harvesting)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P → exponential (Malthusian) growth regime; dP/dt = r*P indicates no density feedback
- Quadratic term in P (P*(1-P/K)) → logistic-type density dependence with a single stable equilibrium at carrying capacity
- Cubic polynomial in P → Allee effect with bistability; indicates both a lower critical threshold and upper carrying capacity
- Logarithmic coupling log(K/P) → Gompertz-type asymmetric growth where deceleration near carrying capacity differs from acceleration at low P
- Fractional power of P (P^alpha with alpha≠1) → allometric/metabolic scaling where per-capita rate depends on body size or colony geometry
- Ratio P/(1+cP) → contest competition or resource saturation where per-capita growth smoothly decreases with crowding
- Product of multiple linear factors in P → multiple equilibria corresponding to extinction, Allee threshold, and carrying capacity
- Explicit time dependence multiplied by population terms → non-autonomous dynamics such as seasonal variation or environmental change
- Sign change in dP/dt at specific P values → equilibrium points; number of zero-crossings indicates number of steady states

## Analysis

The Ground Truth (GT) is:
$$GT = 0.3156 \cdot P \cdot e^{-0.05405t} + \frac{0.3156 \cdot P^2}{9.8709P + 1}$$

This can be rewritten as:
$$GT = 0.3156 \cdot P \cdot e^{-0.05405t} + \frac{0.3156 \cdot P^2}{9.8709P + 1}$$

Now let me check the candidates. The key structure is: a term proportional to $P \cdot e^{-ct}$ and a term $\frac{P^2}{aP+1}$. There's no constant offset term in the GT (setting c0=0 would remove any standalone $P$ term).

**Candidate 60**: $P \cdot c_0 + P \cdot c_1 \cdot e^{c_2 t} + \frac{P \cdot c_3}{P \cdot c_4 + 1}$

Setting $c_0 = 0$, $c_1 = 0.3156$, $c_2 = -0.05405$:
- First two terms give $0.3156 \cdot P \cdot e^{-0.05405t}$ ✓
- Third term: $\frac{P \cdot c_3}{P \cdot c_4 + 1}$. We need this to equal $\frac{0.3156 P^2}{9.8709P + 1}$.
- Setting $c_3 = 0.3156 \cdot P$? No — $c_3$ must be a constant, not depend on $P$.
- $\frac{P \cdot c_3}{P \cdot c_4 + 1} \neq \frac{P^2 \cdot \text{const}}{P \cdot \text{const} + 1}$ since the numerator is $P$ not $P^2$.

So Candidate 60 does NOT match.

**Candidate 20**: $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 e^{c_3 t} + \frac{P c_4}{P c_5 + 1}$

The $P^2 c_0$ term is problematic — it's a standalone $P^2$ term, not $P^2/(aP+1)$.

**Candidate 23**: $\frac{P^2 c_0}{P c_1 + 1} + P c_2 + P c_3 e^{c_4 t} + \frac{P c_5}{P c_6 + 1}$

Set $c_2 = 0$, $c_3 = 0.3156$, $c_4 = -0.05405$, $c_0 = 0.3156$, $c_1 = 9.8709$, $c_5 = 0$:
$$= \frac{0.3156 P^2}{9.8709P + 1} + 0.3156 P e^{-0.05405t}$$

This matches the GT exactly! ✓

**Candidate 37, 38, 39, 42, 44, 45, 47** also have the structure $\frac{P^2}{Pc+1}$ with exponential terms that could potentially match, but Candidate 23 is the simplest clear match.

**Verification of Candidate 23**:
- $\frac{P^2 c_0}{P c_1 + 1}$: with $c_0 = 0.3156$, $c_1 = 9.8709$ → $\frac{0.3156 P^2}{9.8709P + 1}$ ✓
- $P c_2 = 0$ (set $c_2 = 0$) ✓

**Candidate 23 matches the GT.**

**GT:** `0.3156*P*exp(-0.0541*t) + 0.3156*P²/(9.871*P + 1)`

The GT has two terms:
1. `c0*P*exp(-c1*t)` — a P·exp(decay·t) term
2. `c2*P²/(c4*P + c5)` — a rational term P²/(linear in P)

Let me note that `P²/(c4*P + c5)` can be rewritten. Using polynomial division:
`P²/(aP+b) = P/a - b/(a²) + b²/(a²(aP+b))` — this is messy. Let me instead think about what structural forms can match.

The GT can also be written as: `P*exp(-c1*t)*c0 + P*c2*P/(c4*P + c5)`

Note that `P²/(c4*P+1)` can be rewritten using partial fractions:
`P²/(c4*P+1) = P/c4 - 1/c4² + 1/(c4²(c4*P+1))`

So GT = `c0*P*exp(-c1*t) + c2*[P/c4 - 1/c4² + 1/(c4²(c4*P+1))]`
= `c0*P*exp(-c1*t) + (c2/c4)*P - c2/c4² + c2/(c4²(c4*P+1))`

This means GT has the form: `P*exp(·t) + const*P + const + const/(linear in P)`

Now let me check each candidate systematically. I'll focus on which candidates can structurally match.

**Key structural requirement:** The GT needs:
- A `P*exp(αt)` term
- A `P²/(linear in P)` term, which decomposes into `P + const + 1/(linear in P)`

Let me go through candidates, grouping by structure:

**Candidate 60:** `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3/(P*c4 + 1)`

This has `P*c3/(P*c4+1)`. GT needs `P²*c/(P*c4+1)`. These are different: `P/(P*c4+1)` vs `P²/(P*c4+1)`. Can we reconcile?

`P*c3/(P*c4+1)` — this is degree 1/degree 1 rational in P.
`P²/(P*c4+1)` — this is degree 2/degree 1 rational in P.

The `P*c0` term is degree 1. So Candidate 60 gives: `P*(c0 + c1*exp) + P*c3/(Pc4+1)`. The rational part is `P/(Pc4+1)` which behaves like `1/c4` for large P, while GT's rational part `P²/(Pc4+1)` behaves like `P/c4` for large P. These cannot match.

Wait, but the full expression for GT decomposed is: `c0*P*exp(-c1*t) + (c2/c4)*P - c2/c4² + c2/(c4²(c4*P+1))`.

So Candidate 60 needs to provide: `P*const + const + const/(Pc4+1)`. It provides `P*c0 + P*c3/(Pc4+1)`. 

`P*c3/(Pc4+1) = c3*P/(Pc4+1)`. This can be decomposed: `c3/c4 - c3/(c4(Pc4+1))` = `c3/c4 - c3/(c4²P + c4)`.

So Candidate 60 = `P*(c0 + c3/c4) + P*c1*exp(c2*t) - c3/(c4(Pc4+1))`.

GT decomposed = `P*(c2/c4) + c0*P*exp(-c1*t) - c2/c4² + c2/(c4²(c4P+1))`.

Comparing: GT has a constant term `-c2/c4²` and a `+1/(c4P+1)` term. Candidate 60 has a `-1/(c4P+1)` term but no constant. The sign of the `1/(c4P+1)` term differs, and there's a missing constant. So **NO MATCH**.

Let me now focus on candidates that have the right structure. I need candidates that can produce `P²/(linear in P)`.

Decomposing `P*c3/(Pc4+1) = c3/c4 - c3/(c4(Pc4+1))`:

Total = `P*(c0+c5+c3*c4... wait, let me redo.

Actually, `P*c3/(Pc4+1)`: let me do partial fractions properly.
`P/(Pc4+1) = (1/c4) * (Pc4+1-1)/(Pc4+1) = 1/c4 - 1/(c4*(Pc4+1))`

So `P*c3/(Pc4+1) = c3/c4 - c3/(c4*(Pc4+1))`

Candidate 55 = `P*(c0+c5) + c3/c4 + c6 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) - c3/(c4*(Pc4+1))`

GT = `P*(c2_gt/c4_gt) - c2_gt/c4_gt² + c2_gt/(c4_gt²*(c4_gt*P+1)) + c0_gt*P*exp(-c1_gt*t)`

For matching:
- `P*exp` term: ✓ (set c1=c0_gt, c2=-c1_gt)
- `P` coefficient: c0+c5 = c2_gt/c4_gt ✓
- constant: c3/c4 + c6 = -c2_gt/c4_gt²

With c3 = -c2_gt/c4_gt (negative), c4 = c4_gt, c6 = 0, c0+c5 = c2_gt/c4_gt. All constants are free, so this works!

**Candidate 55 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 56:** `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3/(P*c4 + 1) + c5`

Need: P coefficient: c0 = c2_gt/c4_gt
constant: c3/c4 + c5 = -c2_gt/c4_gt²
1/(c4P+1): -c3/c4 = c2_gt/c4_gt², c4 = c4_gt

So c3 = -c2_gt/c4_gt, c4 = c4_gt, c0 = c2_gt/c4_gt, c5 = -c2_gt/c4_gt² - c3/c4 = -c2_gt/c4_gt² + c2_gt/c4_gt² = 0.

All constants determined and consistent. ✓

**Candidate 56 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 33:** `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3/(P*c4 + 1) + c5*t + c6`

Has an extra `c5*t` term. GT has no `t` term (outside the exponential). Set c5=0, then it reduces to Candidate 56. ✓

**Candidate 33 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 26:** `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3/(P*c4 + 1) + c5/(P*c6 + c7)`

Decompose: `P*c0 + P*c1*exp + c3/c4 - c3/(c4(c4P+1)) + c5/(c6P+c7)`

GT needs `1/(c4_gt*P+1)` term. If we set c6 = c4_gt, c7 = 1, then we have two `1/(c4P+1)` terms: `-c3/c4 + c5` divided by `(c4P+1)`. We can combine them. Also need constant and P terms.

Actually: `P*c3/(Pc4+1) + c5/(Pc6+c7)`. If c6*c4_gt... let me set c4 = c4_gt and c6 = c4_gt, c7 = 1.

Then: `P*c3/(c4_gt*P+1) + c5/(c4_gt*P+1) = (c3*P + c5)/(c4_gt*P+1)`

GT's rational part is `c2_gt*P²/(c4_gt*P+1)`. 

`(c3*P + c5)/(c4_gt*P+1)` is degree 1/degree 1, but GT needs degree 2/degree 1. The `P*c0` term adds a free `P` term. Let me combine everything over common denominator:

`P*c0 + (c3*P + c5)/(c4_gt*P+1) = [P*c0*(c4_gt*P+1) + c3*P + c5]/(c4_gt*P+1)`
`= [c0*c4_gt*P² + (c0+c3)*P + c5]/(c4_gt*P+1)`

GT rational part: `c2_gt*P²/(c4_gt*P+1)`. So we need:
- `c0*c4_gt = c2_gt` → c0 = c2_gt/c4_gt ✓
- `c0+c3 = 0` → c3 = -c0 = -c2_gt/c4_gt ✓
- `c5 = 0` ✓

All free constants, works! ✓

**Candidate 26 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 19:** `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3/(P*c4 + 1) + P*c5/(P*c6 + c7) + c8/(P*c6 + c7)`

This has `(P*c5 + c8)/(P*c6+c7)` as extra terms beyond the base. Combined with `P*c3/(Pc4+1)` and `P*c0`, this has more than enough freedom. Set c6=c4, c7=1 (same denominator), then combine:

`P*c3/(Pc4+1) + (Pc5+c8)/(Pc4+1) = (c3P + c5P + c8)/(Pc4+1) = ((c3+c5)P + c8)/(Pc4+1)`

Then `P*c0 + ((c3+c5)P + c8)/(Pc4+1)` over common denominator:
`= [c0*c4*P² + (c0 + c3+c5)*P + c8]/(c4P+1)`

Need: c0*c4 = c2_gt, c0+c3+c5 = 0, c8 = 0. All achievable. ✓

**Candidate 19 verdict: [MATCH]**

Now let me systematically check the remaining candidates. Let me group them:

**Candidates with structure `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3/(P*c4 + 1) + [extra]`:**

These are: 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 10, 11, 12, 15, 18, 20, 21, 22, 25, 33, 35, 40, 48, 49, 55, 56, 60, 69, 70, 71, 77, 78

For all of these, the base `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3/(P*c4+1)` decomposes to:
`P*(c0 + c3*c4/(c4)...) ` — wait, let me just use the decomposition I already did.

Base = `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3/c4 - c3/(c4(c4P+1))`

GT = `P*(c2_gt/c4_gt) + c0_gt*P*exp(-c1_gt*t) - c2_gt/c4_gt² + c2_gt/(c4_gt²(c4_gt*P+1))`

The base already provides: P term, P*exp term, constant term, 1/(c4P+1) term.

But the issue is: the base has 4 unknowns (c0, c1, c2, c3, c4 = 5 unknowns) and needs to match 4 conditions:
1. P coefficient: c0 = c2_gt/c4_gt
2. exp term: c1, c2 match
3. constant: c3/c4 = -c2_gt/c4_gt²
4. 1/(c4P+1) term: c4 = c4_gt and -c3/c4 = c2_gt/c4_gt²

From (4): c3 = -c2_gt/c4_gt, c4 = c4_gt
From (3): c3/c4 = -c2_gt/c4_gt² ✓ (consistent)

So the base alone (Candidate 60) already matches GT if we can accept the constant term. Wait:

Base constant = c3/c4 = (-c2_gt/c4_gt)/c4_gt = -c2_gt/c4_gt²

GT constant = -c2_gt/c4_gt²

These are equal! So Candidate 60 actually matches!

Wait, let me recheck. The base `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3/(P*c4+1)`:

Decompose `P*c3/(Pc4+1)`:
`= c3*P/(c4P+1) = (c3/c4)*(c4P+1-1)/(c4P+1) = c3/c4 - c3/(c4(c4P+1))`

So base = `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3/c4 - c3/(c4(c4P+1))`

GT = `c0_gt*P*exp(-c1_gt*t) + c2_gt*P²/(c4_gt*P+1)`

Decompose GT's rational: `c2_gt*P²/(c4_gt*P+1)`:
`= (c2_gt/c4_gt)*P*(c4_gt*P+1-1)/(c4_gt*P+1) = (c2_gt/c4_gt)*P - (c2_gt/c4_gt)*P/(c4_gt*P+1)`
`= (c2_gt/c4_gt)*P - (c2_gt/c4_gt²)*(c4_gt*P+1-1)/(c4_gt*P+1)`
`= (c2_gt/c4_gt)*P - c2_gt/c4_gt² + c2_gt/(c4_gt²(c4_gt*P+1))`

So GT = `c0_gt*P*exp(-c1_gt*t) + (c2_gt/c4_gt)*P - c2_gt/c4_gt² + c2_gt/(c4_gt²(c4_gt*P+1))`

Base = `c0*P + c1*P*exp(c2*t) + c3/c4 - c3/(c4(c4*P+1))`

Matching:
- P*exp: c1=c0_gt, c2=-c1_gt ✓
- P: c0 = c2_gt/c4_gt ✓
- constant: c3/c4 = -c2_gt/c4_gt² 
- 1/(c4P+1): need c4=c4_gt and -c3/c4 = c2_gt/c4_gt²

From the last: c3 = -c2_gt/c4_gt, so c3/c4 = -c2_gt/c4_gt². ✓ Consistent!

So **Candidate 60 matches!**

**Candidate 60 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 29:** `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(c4/P) + c5*t/(P*c6 + c7) + c8/(P*c6 + c7)`

Set c3=0, c5=0: `P*c0 + P*c1*exp + c8/(Pc6+c7)`. This is Candidate 26 structure (without the `P*c3/(Pc4+1)` but with `c8/(Pc6+c7)`).

Over common denominator: `[c0*(c6P+c7)*P + c8]/(c6P+c7) + P*c1*exp`
`= [c0*c6*P² + c0*c7*P + c8]/(c6P+c7) + P*c1*exp`

Need: c0*c6 = c2_gt, c0*c7 = 0, c8 = 0, c6 = c4_gt, c7 = 1.
But c0*c7 = c0*1 = c0 = 0, then c0*c6 = 0 ≠ c2_gt. Contradiction.

What if c7 = 0? Then denominator is c6*P, and we get `c0*c6*P² + c8]/(c6*P)` = `c0*P + c8/(c6P)`. The `c8/(c6P)` = `const/P` which is not in GT.

What about keeping c3 ≠ 0? Then we have `exp(c4/P)` which can't match rational functions.

What about c5 ≠ 0? `c5*t/(Pc6+c7)` introduces t-dependence in the rational part, which GT doesn't have.

Actually wait, let me reconsider. We have `c5*t/(Pc6+c7) + c8/(Pc6+c7) = (c5*t + c8)/(Pc6+c7)`. This is t-dependent. GT's rational part is t-independent. So c5 must be 0.

With c5=0: `P*c0 + P*c1*exp + c3*exp(c4/P) + c8/(Pc6+c7)`.

`exp(c4/P)` cannot be combined with the other terms to form `P²/(aP+b)`. Setting c3=0 leaves us short as shown above.

**Candidate 29 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 30:** `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*exp(c6/P)`

**Candidate 36:** `P²*c0/(Pc1+c2) + P²*c3*log(c4*exp(c5*t)+1)/(Pc1+c2) + P*c6/(Pc1+c2) + P*c7*log(c4*exp(c5*t)+1)/(Pc1+c2) + c8/(Pc1+c2)`

`= [P²*c0 + P²*c3*log(...) + P*c6 + P*c7*log(...) + c8] / (Pc1+c2)`
`= [P²*(c0 + c3*log(...)) + P*(c6 + c7*log(...)) + c8] / (Pc1+c2)`

GT = `c0_gt*P*exp(-c1_gt*t) + c2_gt*P²/(c4_gt*P+1)`

The `log(c4*exp(c5*t)+1)` is NOT equivalent to `exp(αt)` for any constants. It's a softplus function. So this candidate uses log-based t-dependence instead of pure exponential. These are linearly independent functions.

Can we set c3=0, c7=0? Then: `[P²*c0 + P*c6 + c8]/(Pc1+c2)`. This is a rational function of P only, no t-dependence. But GT needs a `P*exp(αt)` term. So this can't match.

**Candidate 36 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

**Candidate 37:** `[P²*c0 + P²*c2*exp(c3*t) + P*c4 + P*c5*exp(c3*t) + c6] / (Pc1+1)`

`= [P²*(c0+c2*exp(c3t)) + P*(c4+c5*exp(c3t)) + c6] / (c1P+1)`

GT = `c0_gt*P*exp(-c1_gt*t) + c2_gt*P²/(c4_gt*P+1)`

Let me try to match. Set c1=c4_gt. Then:

`= [P²*(c0+c2*exp) + P*(c4+c5*exp) + c6] / (c4_gt*P+1)`

GT over same denominator: `c0_gt*P*exp*(-c1_gt*t)*(c4_gt*P+1) + c2_gt*P²`
`= c0_gt*c4_gt*P²*exp + c0_gt*P*exp + c2_gt*P²`
`= P²*(c2_gt + c0_gt*c4_gt*exp) + P*c0_gt*exp`

So numerator of GT = `P²*(c2_gt + c0_gt*c4_gt*exp(-c1_gt*t)) + P*c0_gt*exp(-c1_gt*t) + 0`

Candidate numerator = `P²*(c0+c2*exp(c3t)) + P*(c4+c5*exp(c3t)) + c6`

Matching:
- P² constant: c0 = c2_gt ✓
- P² exp: c2*exp(c3t) = c0_gt*c4_gt*exp(-c1_gt*t) → c2=c0_gt*c4_gt, c3=-c1_gt ✓
- P constant: c4 = 0 ✓
- P exp: c5*exp(c3t) = c0_gt*exp(-c1_gt*t) → c5=c0_gt ✓ (c3 already set)
- constant: c6 = 0 ✓

All consistent! ✓

**Candidate 37 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 38:** Same as 37 with extra `P*c6/(Pc1+1) + P*c7/(Pc1+1) + c8/(Pc1+1)`. These add `P*(c6+c7) + c8` to the numerator. Set c6=0, c7=0, c8=0 (or absorb into existing terms). ✓

Actually wait, Candidate 38 = `P²*c0/(Pc1+1) + P²*c2*exp(c3t)/(Pc1+1) + P*c4/(Pc1+1) + P*c5*exp(c3t)/(Pc1+1) + P*c6/(Pc1+1) + P*c7/(Pc1+1) + c8/(Pc1+1)`

Hmm, this gets complicated. Let me think differently.

`P²*c0/(c1P+1)` decomposes as: `(c0/c1)*P - c0/c1² + c0/(c1²(c1P+1))`

So total = `(c0/c1 + c2)*P + c3*P*exp + (-c0/c1² + c5) + c0/(c1²(c1P+1))`

GT = `(c2_gt/c4_gt)*P + c0_gt*P*exp + (-c2_gt/c4_gt²) + c2_gt/(c4_gt²(c4_gt*P+1))`

Matching:
- c1 = c4_gt ✓
- c0/c1 + c2 = c2_gt/c4_gt → c0/c4_gt + c2 = c2_gt/c4_gt ✓
- c3, c4 match exp ✓
- -c0/c1² + c5 = -c2_gt/c4_gt² → c5 = -c2_gt/c4_gt² + c0/c4_gt² ✓
- c0/c1² = c2_gt/c4_gt² → c0 = c2_gt ✓

Then c2 = c2_gt/c4_gt - c2_gt/c4_gt = 0, c5 = 0. All consistent. ✓
